## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task seeks a constitutive relation σ(ε, T) describing how stress depends on strain and temperature. Temperature typically causes thermal softening (reducing elastic modulus and flow stress), while strain causes hardening, often following power-law or saturating forms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at small strains)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic deformation)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic transition)
- Johnson-Cook strength model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal softening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain hardening and thermal effects)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-like thermal activation with power-law hardening)
- Ludwik equation with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (yield stress plus hardening with thermal factor)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening avoiding singularity at zero strain)
- Temperature-dependent Swift: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (1 + c3 * T) (Swift hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Saturating stress model: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (epsilon + c1) * (1 + c2 * T) (Michaelis-Menten-like saturation with thermal factor)
- Polynomial thermal modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature dependence of elastic modulus)
- Hyperbolic tangent hardening: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (smooth saturating hardening with thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening (increasing stress with strain at decreasing rate) → Power-law epsilon**c with 0<c<1, or saturating forms like 1-exp(-c*epsilon)
- Thermal softening (decreasing stress with temperature) → Multiplicative factor exp(c*T) with c<0, or (1 - c*T), or T**c with c<0
- Elastic-plastic transition → Additive terms: linear term c0*epsilon plus nonlinear hardening term c1*epsilon**c2
- Separable thermo-mechanical response → Product form f(epsilon) * g(T), where strain and temperature effects factorize
- Yield stress offset → Constant term c0 added to strain-dependent hardening: sigma = c0 + f(epsilon)
- Singularity avoidance at zero strain → Shifted power law (epsilon + c)**n instead of epsilon**n
- Rate-independent thermal activation → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or exp(c*T) multiplicative factors on flow stress
- Non-monotonic temperature effects → Quadratic or polynomial temperature terms (c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2)
